    <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M8.22 1.754a.25.25 0 00-.44 0L1.698 13.132a.25.25 0 00.22.368h12.164a.25.25 0 00.22-.368L8.22 1.754zm-1.763-.707c.659-1.234 2.427-1.234 3.086 0l6.082 11.378A1.75 1.75 0 0114.082 15H1.918a1.75 1.75 0 01-1.543-2.575L6.457 1.047zM9 11a1 1 0 11-2 0 1 1 0 012 0zm-.25-5.25a.75.75 0 00-1.5 0v2.5a.75.75 0 001.5 0v-2.5z"></path>

        <div id="readme" class="Box-body readme blob js-code-block-container p-5 p-xl-6 gist-border-0">
    <article class="markdown-body entry-content container-lg" itemprop="text"><table>
  <thead>
  <tr>
  <th>title</th>
  <th>author</th>
  <th>date</th>
  </tr>
  </thead>
  <tbody>
  <tr>
  <td><div dir="auto">Functional Analysis for RNA-seq</div></td>
  <td><div dir="auto">Mary Piper</div></td>
  <td><div dir="auto">Tuesday, March 20th, 2018</div></td>
  </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

<p dir="auto">Approximate time: 120 minutes</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-learning-objectives" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#learning-objectives"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Learning Objectives:</h2>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Determine how functions are attributed to genes using Gene Ontology terms</li>
<li>Understand the theory of how functional enrichment tools yield statistically enriched functions or interactions</li>
<li>Discuss functional analysis using over-representation analysis, functional class scoring, and pathway topology methods</li>
<li>Explore functional analysis tools</li>
</ul>
<h1 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-functional-analysis" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#functional-analysis"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Functional analysis</h1>
<p dir="auto">The output of RNA-seq differential expression analysis is a list of significant differentially expressed genes (DEGs). To gain greater biological insight on the differentially expressed genes there are various analyses that can be done:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>determine whether there is enrichment of known biological functions, interactions, or pathways</li>
<li>identify genes' involvement in novel pathways or networks by grouping genes together based on similar trends</li>
<li>use global changes in gene expression by visualizing all genes being significantly up- or down-regulated in the context of external interaction data</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Generally for any differential expression analysis, it is useful to interpret the resulting gene lists using freely available web- and R-based tools.  While tools for functional analysis span a wide variety of techniques, they can loosely be categorized into three main types: over-representation analysis, functional class scoring, and pathway topology [<a href="https://github.com/hbctraining/In-depth-NGS-Data-Analysis-Course/raw/master/resources/pathway_tools.pdf">1</a>].</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/pathway_analysis.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/pathway_analysis.png" alt="Pathway analysis tools" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The goal of functional analysis is provide biological insight, so it's necessary to analyze our results in the context of our experimental hypothesis: <strong>FMRP and MOV10 associate and regulate the translation of a subset of RNAs</strong>. Therefore, based on the authors' hypothesis, we may expect the enrichment of processes/pathways related to <strong>translation, splicing, and the regulation of mRNAs</strong>, which we would need to validate experimentally.</p>
<p dir="auto"><em><strong>Note that all tools described below are great tools to validate experimental results and to make hypotheses. These tools suggest genes/pathways that may be involved with your condition of interest; however, you should NOT use these tools to make conclusions about the pathways involved in your experimental process. You will need to perform experimental validation of any suggested pathways.</strong></em></p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-over-representation-analysis" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#over-representation-analysis"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Over-representation analysis</h2>
<p dir="auto">There are a plethora of functional enrichment tools that perform some type of "over-representation" analysis by querying databases containing information about gene function and interactions.</p>
<p dir="auto">These databases typically categorize genes into groups based on shared function, or involvement in a pathway, or presence in a specific cellular location, or other categorizations, e.g. functional pathways, etc. Essentially, known genes are binned into categories that have been consistently named (controlled vocabulary) based on how the gene has been annotated functionally. These categories are independent of any organism, however each organism has distinct categorizations available.</p>
<p dir="auto">To determine whether any categories are over-represented, you can determine the probability of having the observed proportion of genes associated with a specific category in your gene list based on the proportion of genes associated with the same category in the background set (gene categorizations for the appropriate organism).</p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/go_proportions.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/go_proportions.png" width="600" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/go_proportions_table3.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/go_proportions_table3.png" width="600" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The statistical test that will determine whether something is actually over-represented is the <em>Hypergeometric test</em>.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-hypergeometric-testing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#hypergeometric-testing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Hypergeometric testing</h3>
<p dir="auto">Using the example of the first functional category above, hypergeometric distribution is a probability distribution that describes the probability of 25 genes (k) being associated with "Functional category 1", for all genes in our gene list (n=1000), from a population of all of the genes in entire genome (N=13,000) which contains 35 genes (K) associated with "Functional category 1" [<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypergeometric_distribution" rel="nofollow">4</a>].</p>
<p dir="auto">The calculation of probability of k successes follows the formula:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/hypergeo.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/hypergeo.png" alt="hypergeo" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">This test will result in an adjusted p-value (after multiple test correction) for each category tested.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-gene-ontology-project" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#gene-ontology-project"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Gene Ontology project</h3>
<p dir="auto">One of the most widely-used categorizations is the <strong>Gene Ontology (GO)</strong> established by the Gene Ontology project.</p>
<p dir="auto">"The Gene Ontology project is a collaborative effort to address the need for consistent descriptions of gene products across databases" [<a href="http://geneontology.org/page/introduction-go-resource" rel="nofollow">2</a>]. The <a href="http://geneontology.org/page/go-consortium-contributors-list" rel="nofollow">Gene Ontology Consortium</a> maintains the GO terms, and these GO terms are incorporated into gene annotations in many of the popular repositories for animal, plant, and microbial genomes.</p>
<p dir="auto">Tools that investigate enrichment of biological functions or interactions often use the Gene Ontology (GO) categorizations, i.e. the GO terms to determine whether any have significantly modified representation in a given list of genes. Therefore, to best use and interpret the results from these functional analysis tools, it is helpful to have a good understanding of the GO terms themselves and their organization.</p>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-go-ontologies" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#go-ontologies"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>GO Ontologies</h4>
<p dir="auto">To describe the roles of genes and gene products, GO terms are organized into three independent controlled vocabularies (ontologies) in a species-independent manner:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Biological process:</strong> refers to the biological role involving the gene or gene product, and could include "transcription", "signal transduction", and "apoptosis". A biological process generally involves a chemical or physical change of the starting material or input.</li>
<li><strong>Molecular function:</strong> represents the biochemical activity of the gene product, such activities could include "ligand", "GTPase", and "transporter".</li>
<li><strong>Cellular component:</strong> refers to the location in the cell of the gene product. Cellular components could include "nucleus", "lysosome", and "plasma membrane".</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Each GO term has a term name (e.g. <strong>DNA repair</strong>) and a unique term accession number (<strong>GO:0005125</strong>), and a single gene product can be associated with many GO terms, since a single gene product "may function in several processes, contain domains that carry out diverse molecular functions, and participate in multiple alternative interactions with other proteins, organelles or locations in the cell" [<a href="https://github.com/hbctraining/In-depth-NGS-Data-Analysis-Course/raw/master/resources/go_terms.pdf">3</a>].</p>
<h4 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-go-term-hierarchy" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#go-term-hierarchy"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>GO term hierarchy</h4>
<p dir="auto">Some gene products are well-researched, with vast quantities of data available regarding their biological processes and functions. However, other gene products have very little data available about their roles in the cell.</p>
<p dir="auto">For example, the protein, "p53", would contain a wealth of information on it's roles in the cell, whereas another protein might only be known as a "membrane-bound protein" with no other information available.</p>
<p dir="auto">The GO ontologies were developed to describe and query biological knowledge with differing levels of information available. To do this, GO ontologies are loosely hierarchical, ranging from general, 'parent', terms to more specific, 'child' terms. The GO ontologies are "loosely" hierarchical since 'child' terms can have multiple 'parent' terms.</p>
<p dir="auto">Some genes with less information may only be associated with general 'parent' terms or no terms at all, while other genes with a lot of information be associated with many terms.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/go_heirarchy.jpg"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/go_heirarchy.jpg" alt="Nature Reviews Cancer 7, 23-34 (January 2007)" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto"><a href="http://journals.plos.org/ploscompbiol/article?id=10.1371/journal.pcbi.1003343" rel="nofollow">Tips for working with GO terms</a></p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-clusterprofiler" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#clusterprofiler"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>clusterProfiler</h2>
<p dir="auto">We will be using <a href="http://bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/clusterProfiler.html" rel="nofollow">clusterProfiler</a> to perform over-representation analysis on GO terms associated with our list of significant genes. The tool takes as input a significant gene list and a background gene list and performs statistical enrichment analysis using hypergeometric testing. The basic arguments allow the user to select the appropriate organism and GO ontology (BP, CC, MF) to test.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-running-clusterprofiler" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#running-clusterprofiler"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Running clusterProfiler</h3>
<p dir="auto">To run clusterProfiler GO over-representation analysis, we will change our gene names into Ensembl IDs, since the tool works a bit easier with the Ensembl IDs.</p>
<p dir="auto">Let's open up our previous <strong><code>DEanalysis</code> project</strong>, and create a <strong><code>functional_analysis.R</code> script</strong>.</p>
<p dir="auto">Then load the following libraries:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="library(org.Hs.eg.db)
library(DOSE)
library(pathview)
library(clusterProfiler)
library(AnnotationHub)
library(ensembldb)
library(tidyverse)"><pre>library(<span class="pl-smi">org.Hs.eg.db</span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">DOSE</span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">pathview</span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">clusterProfiler</span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">AnnotationHub</span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">ensembldb</span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">tidyverse</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">For the different steps in the functional analysis, we require Ensembl and Entrez IDs. To convert the gene symbols to these IDs, we will use the <strong>annotables</strong> package and merge the IDs with the DE results.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Explore the grch37 table loaded by the annotables library
grch37

## Return the IDs for the gene symbols in the DE results
idx &lt;- grch37$symbol %in% rownames(res_tableOE)

ids &lt;- grch37[idx, ]

## The gene names can map to more than one Ensembl ID (some genes change ID over time), 
## so we need to remove duplicate IDs prior to assessing enriched GO terms
non_duplicates &lt;- which(duplicated(ids$symbol) == FALSE)

ids &lt;- ids[non_duplicates, ] 

## Merge the IDs with the results 
res_ids &lt;- inner_join(res_tableOE_tb, ids, by=c(&quot;gene&quot;=&quot;symbol&quot;))         "><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Explore the grch37 table loaded by the annotables library</span>
<span class="pl-smi">grch37</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Return the IDs for the gene symbols in the DE results</span>
<span class="pl-smi">idx</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">grch37</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">symbol</span> <span class="pl-k">%in%</span> rownames(<span class="pl-smi">res_tableOE</span>)

<span class="pl-smi">ids</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">grch37</span>[<span class="pl-smi">idx</span>, ]

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># The gene names can map to more than one Ensembl ID (some genes change ID over time), </span>
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># so we need to remove duplicate IDs prior to assessing enriched GO terms</span>
<span class="pl-smi">non_duplicates</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> which(duplicated(<span class="pl-smi">ids</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">symbol</span>) <span class="pl-k">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">FALSE</span>)

<span class="pl-smi">ids</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">ids</span>[<span class="pl-smi">non_duplicates</span>, ] 

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Merge the IDs with the results </span>
<span class="pl-smi">res_ids</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> inner_join(<span class="pl-smi">res_tableOE_tb</span>, <span class="pl-smi">ids</span>, <span class="pl-v">by</span><span class="pl-k">=</span>c(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>gene<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>symbol<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>))         </pre></div>
<p dir="auto">To perform the over-representation analysis, we need a list of background genes and a list of significant genes. For our background dataset we will use all genes tested for differential expression (all genes in our results table). For our significant gene list we will use genes with p-adjusted values less than 0.05 (we could include a fold change threshold too if we have many DE genes).</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Create background dataset for hypergeometric testing using all genes tested for significance in the results                 
allOE_genes &lt;- as.character(res_ids$ensgene)

## Extract significant results
sigOE &lt;- filter(res_ids, padj &lt; 0.05)

sigOE_genes &lt;- as.character(sigOE$ensgene)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Create background dataset for hypergeometric testing using all genes tested for significance in the results                 </span>
<span class="pl-smi">allOE_genes</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> as.character(<span class="pl-smi">res_ids</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">ensgene</span>)

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Extract significant results</span>
<span class="pl-smi">sigOE</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> filter(<span class="pl-smi">res_ids</span>, <span class="pl-smi">padj</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">0.05</span>)

<span class="pl-smi">sigOE_genes</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> as.character(<span class="pl-smi">sigOE</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">ensgene</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Now we can perform the GO enrichment analysis and save the results:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Run GO enrichment analysis 
ego &lt;- enrichGO(gene = sigOE_genes, 
                universe = allOE_genes,
                keyType = &quot;ENSEMBL&quot;,
                OrgDb = org.Hs.eg.db, 
                ont = &quot;BP&quot;, 
                pAdjustMethod = &quot;BH&quot;, 
                qvalueCutoff = 0.05, 
                readable = TRUE)
                
## Output results from GO analysis to a table
cluster_summary &lt;- data.frame(ego)

write.csv(cluster_summary, &quot;results/clusterProfiler_Mov10oe.csv&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Run GO enrichment analysis </span>
<span class="pl-smi">ego</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> enrichGO(<span class="pl-v">gene</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">sigOE_genes</span>, 
                <span class="pl-v">universe</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">allOE_genes</span>,
                <span class="pl-v">keyType</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>ENSEMBL<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>,
                <span class="pl-v">OrgDb</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">org.Hs.eg.db</span>, 
                <span class="pl-v">ont</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>BP<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, 
                <span class="pl-v">pAdjustMethod</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>BH<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, 
                <span class="pl-v">qvalueCutoff</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0.05</span>, 
                <span class="pl-v">readable</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">TRUE</span>)
                
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Output results from GO analysis to a table</span>
<span class="pl-smi">cluster_summary</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-k">data.frame</span>(<span class="pl-smi">ego</span>)

write.csv(<span class="pl-smi">cluster_summary</span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>results/clusterProfiler_Mov10oe.csv<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)</pre></div>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE:</strong> The different organisms with annotation databases available to use with clusterProfiler can be found <a href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/orgdb_annotation_databases.png">here</a>
Also, the <code>keyType</code> argument may be coded as <code>keytype</code> in different versions of clusterProfiler.</p>
</blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/cluster_summary.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/cluster_summary.png" alt="cluster_summary" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-visualizing-clusterprofiler-results" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#visualizing-clusterprofiler-results"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Visualizing clusterProfiler results</h3>
<p dir="auto">clusterProfiler has a variety of options for viewing the over-represented GO terms. We will explore the dotplot, enrichment plot, and the category netplot.</p>
<p dir="auto">The <strong>dotplot</strong> shows the number of genes associated with the first 50 terms (size) and the p-adjusted values for these terms (color). This plot displays the top 50 genes by gene ratio (# genes related to GO term / total number of sig genes), not p-adjusted value.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Dotplot 
dotplot(ego, showCategory=50)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Dotplot </span>
dotplot(<span class="pl-smi">ego</span>, <span class="pl-v">showCategory</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">50</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>To save the figure,</strong> click on the <code>Export</code> button in the RStudio <code>Plots</code> tab and <code>Save as PDF...</code>. In the pop-up window, change:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>Orientation:</code> to <code>Landscape</code></li>
<li><code>PDF size</code> to <code>8 x 14</code> to give a figure of appropriate size for the text labels</li>
</ul>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/mov10oe_dotplot.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/mov10oe_dotplot.png" width="600" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The next plot is the <strong>enrichment GO plot</strong>, which shows the relationship between the top 50 most significantly enriched GO terms (padj.), by grouping similar terms together. The color represents the p-values relative to the other displayed terms (brighter red is more significant) and the size of the terms represents the number of genes that are significant from our list.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Enrichmap clusters the 50 most significant (by padj) GO terms to visualize relationships between terms
emapplot(ego, showCategory = 50)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Enrichmap clusters the 50 most significant (by padj) GO terms to visualize relationships between terms</span>
emapplot(<span class="pl-smi">ego</span>, <span class="pl-v">showCategory</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">50</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>To save the figure,</strong> click on the <code>Export</code> button in the RStudio <code>Plots</code> tab and <code>Save as PDF...</code>. In the pop-up window, change the <code>PDF size</code> to <code>24 x 32</code> to give a figure of appropriate size for the text labels.</p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/mov10oe_enrichmap.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/mov10oe_enrichmap.png" width="800" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Finally, the <strong>category netplot</strong> shows the relationships between the genes associated with the top five most significant GO terms and the fold changes of the significant genes associated with these terms (color). The size of the GO terms reflects the pvalues of the terms, with the more significant terms being larger. This plot is particularly useful for hypothesis generation in identifying genes that may be important to several of the most affected processes.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## To color genes by log2 fold changes, we need to extract the log2 fold changes from our results table creating a named vector
OE_foldchanges &lt;- sigOE$log2FoldChange

names(OE_foldchanges) &lt;- sigOE$gene

## Cnetplot details the genes associated with one or more terms - by default gives the top 5 significant terms (by padj)
cnetplot(ego, 
         categorySize=&quot;pvalue&quot;, 
         showCategory = 5, 
         foldChange=OE_foldchanges, 
         vertex.label.font=6)
         
## If some of the high fold changes are getting drowned out due to a large range, you could set a maximum fold change value
OE_foldchanges &lt;- ifelse(OE_foldchanges &gt; 2, 2, OE_foldchanges)
OE_foldchanges &lt;- ifelse(OE_foldchanges &lt; -2, -2, OE_foldchanges)

cnetplot(ego, 
         categorySize=&quot;pvalue&quot;, 
         showCategory = 5, 
         foldChange=OE_foldchanges, 
         vertex.label.font=6)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># To color genes by log2 fold changes, we need to extract the log2 fold changes from our results table creating a named vector</span>
<span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">sigOE</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">log2FoldChange</span>

names(<span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span>) <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">sigOE</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">gene</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Cnetplot details the genes associated with one or more terms - by default gives the top 5 significant terms (by padj)</span>
cnetplot(<span class="pl-smi">ego</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">categorySize</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>pvalue<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">showCategory</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">5</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">foldChange</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">vertex.label.font</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">6</span>)
         
<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># If some of the high fold changes are getting drowned out due to a large range, you could set a maximum fold change value</span>
<span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> ifelse(<span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span>)
<span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> ifelse(<span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span> <span class="pl-k">-</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-k">-</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span>)

cnetplot(<span class="pl-smi">ego</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">categorySize</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>pvalue<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">showCategory</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">5</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">foldChange</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">vertex.label.font</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">6</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Again, to save the figure,</strong> click on the <code>Export</code> button in the RStudio <code>Plots</code> tab and <code>Save as PDF...</code>. Change the <code>PDF size</code> to <code>24 x 32</code> to give a figure of appropriate size for the text labels.</p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/mov10oe_cnetplot.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/mov10oe_cnetplot.png" width="800" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">If you are interested in significant processes that are <strong>not</strong> among the top five, you can subset your <code>ego</code> dataset to only display these processes:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Subsetting the ego results without overwriting original `ego` variable
ego2 &lt;- ego

ego2@result &lt;- ego@result[c(1,3,4,8,9),]

## Plotting terms of interest
cnetplot(ego2, 
         categorySize=&quot;pvalue&quot;, 
         foldChange=OE_foldchanges, 
         showCategory = 5, 
         vertex.label.font=6)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Subsetting the ego results without overwriting original `ego` variable</span>
<span class="pl-smi">ego2</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">ego</span>

<span class="pl-smi">ego2</span><span class="pl-k">@</span><span class="pl-smi">result</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">ego</span><span class="pl-k">@</span><span class="pl-smi">result</span>[c(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">3</span>,<span class="pl-c1">4</span>,<span class="pl-c1">8</span>,<span class="pl-c1">9</span>),]

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Plotting terms of interest</span>
cnetplot(<span class="pl-smi">ego2</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">categorySize</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>pvalue<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">foldChange</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-smi">OE_foldchanges</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">showCategory</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">5</span>, 
         <span class="pl-v">vertex.label.font</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">6</span>)</pre></div>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/mov10oe_cnetplot2.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/mov10oe_cnetplot2.png" width="800" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-gprofiler" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#gprofiler"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>gProfiler</h3>
<p dir="auto"><a href="http://biit.cs.ut.ee/gprofiler/index.cgi" rel="nofollow">gProfileR</a> is another tool for performing ORA, similar to clusterProfiler. gProfileR considers multiple sources of functional evidence, including Gene Ontology terms, biological pathways, regulatory motifs of transcription factors and microRNAs, human disease annotations and protein-protein interactions. The user selects the organism and the sources of evidence to test. There are also additional parameters to change various thresholds and tweak the stringency to the desired level.</p>
<p dir="auto">The GO terms output by gprofileR are generally quite similar to those output by clusterProfiler, but there are small differences due to the different algorithms used by the tools. We often use gProfiler with <a href="http://revigo.irb.hr/" rel="nofollow">REVIGO</a> to collapse redundant GO terms by semantic similarity and summarize them graphically. If you are interested in exploring gProfileR/REVIGO on your own, we have provided the <a href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/lessons/functional_analysis_other_methods.md">instructional materials</a>.</p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/revigo_treemap.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/revigo_treemap.png" width="800" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">Over-representation analysis is only a single type of functional analysis method that is available for teasing apart the biological processes important to your condition of interest. Other types of analyses can be equally important or informative, including functional class scoring and pathway topology methods.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/pathway_analysis.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/pathway_analysis.png" alt="Pathway analysis tools" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-functional-class-scoring-tools" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#functional-class-scoring-tools"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Functional class scoring tools</h2>
<p dir="auto">Functional class scoring (FCS) tools, such as <a href="http://software.broadinstitute.org/gsea/index.jsp" rel="nofollow">GSEA</a>, most often use the gene-level statistics or log2 fold changes for all genes from the differential expression results, then look to see whether gene sets for particular biological pathways are enriched among the large positive or negative fold changes.</p>
<p><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/gsea_theory.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/gsea_theory.png" width="600" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The hypothesis of FCS methods is that although large changes in individual genes can have significant effects on pathways (and will be detected via ORA methods), weaker but coordinated changes in sets of functionally related genes (i.e., pathways) can also have significant effects.  Thus, rather than setting an arbitrary threshold to identify 'significant genes', <strong>all genes are considered</strong> in the analysis. The gene-level statistics from the dataset are aggregated to generate a single pathway-level statistic and statistical significance of each pathway is reported. This type of analysis can be particularly helpful if the differential expression analysis only outputs a small list of significant DE genes.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-gene-set-enrichment-analysis-using-clusterprofiler-and-pathview" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#gene-set-enrichment-analysis-using-clusterprofiler-and-pathview"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Gene set enrichment analysis using clusterProfiler and Pathview</h3>
<p dir="auto">Using the log2 fold changes obtained from the differential expression analysis for every gene, gene set enrichment analysis and pathway analysis can be performed using clusterProfiler and Pathview tools.</p>
<p dir="auto">For gene set or pathway analysis using clusterProfiler, coordinated differential expression over gene sets is tested instead of changes of individual genes. "Gene sets are pre-defined groups of genes, which are functionally related. Commonly used gene sets include those derived from KEGG pathways, Gene Ontology terms, MSigDB, Reactome, or gene groups that share some other functional annotations, etc. Consistent perturbations over such gene sets frequently suggest mechanistic changes" [<a href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/resources/pathway_tools.pdf">1</a>].</p>
<p dir="auto">To perform GSEA analysis of KEGG gene sets, clusterProfiler requires the genes to be identified using Entrez IDs for all genes in our results dataset. We also need to remove the NA values and duplicates (due to gene ID conversion) prior to the analysis:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Remove any NA values
res_entrez &lt;- filter(res_ids, entrez != &quot;NA&quot;)

## Remove any Entrez duplicates
res_entrez &lt;- res_entrez[which(duplicated(res_entrez$entrez) == F), ]
"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Remove any NA values</span>
<span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> filter(<span class="pl-smi">res_ids</span>, <span class="pl-smi">entrez</span> <span class="pl-k">!=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>NA<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Remove any Entrez duplicates</span>
<span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span>[which(duplicated(<span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">entrez</span>) <span class="pl-k">==</span> <span class="pl-c1">F</span>), ]
</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Finally, extract and name the fold changes:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Extract the foldchanges
foldchanges &lt;- res_entrez$log2FoldChange

## Name each fold change with the corresponding Entrez ID
names(foldchanges) &lt;- res_entrez$entrez"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Extract the foldchanges</span>
<span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">log2FoldChange</span>

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Name each fold change with the corresponding Entrez ID</span>
names(<span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span>) <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">entrez</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Next we need to order the fold changes in decreasing order. To do this we'll use the <code>sort()</code> function, which takes a vector as input. This is in contrast to Tidyverse's <code>arrange()</code>, which requires a data frame.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Sort fold changes in decreasing order
foldchanges &lt;- sort(foldchanges, decreasing = TRUE)

head(foldchanges)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Sort fold changes in decreasing order</span>
<span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> sort(<span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span>, <span class="pl-v">decreasing</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">TRUE</span>)

head(<span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Perform the GSEA using KEGG gene sets:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## GSEA using gene sets from KEGG pathways
gseaKEGG &lt;- gseKEGG(geneList = foldchanges, # ordered named vector of fold changes (Entrez IDs are the associated names)
              organism = &quot;hsa&quot;, # supported organisms listed below
              nPerm = 1000, # default number permutations
              minGSSize = 20, # minimum gene set size (# genes in set) - change to test more sets or recover sets with fewer # genes
              pvalueCutoff = 0.05, # padj cutoff value
              verbose = FALSE)

## Extract the GSEA results
gseaKEGG_results &lt;- gseaKEGG@result"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># GSEA using gene sets from KEGG pathways</span>
<span class="pl-smi">gseaKEGG</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> gseKEGG(<span class="pl-v">geneList</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span>, <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> ordered named vector of fold changes (Entrez IDs are the associated names)</span>
              <span class="pl-v">organism</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>hsa<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> supported organisms listed below</span>
              <span class="pl-v">nPerm</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">1000</span>, <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> default number permutations</span>

              <span class="pl-v">pvalueCutoff</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">0.05</span>, <span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> padj cutoff value</span>
              <span class="pl-v">verbose</span> <span class="pl-k">=</span> <span class="pl-c1">FALSE</span>)

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Extract the GSEA results</span>
<span class="pl-smi">gseaKEGG_results</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">gseaKEGG</span><span class="pl-k">@</span><span class="pl-smi">result</span></pre></div>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE:</strong> The organisms with KEGG pathway information are listed <a href="http://www.genome.jp/kegg/catalog/org_list.html" rel="nofollow">here</a>.</p>
</blockquote>
<p dir="auto">View the enriched pathways:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Write GSEA results to file
View(gseaKEGG_results)

write.csv(gseaKEGG_results, &quot;results/gseaOE_kegg.csv&quot;, quote=F)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Write GSEA results to file</span>
View(<span class="pl-smi">gseaKEGG_results</span>)

write.csv(<span class="pl-smi">gseaKEGG_results</span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>results/gseaOE_kegg.csv<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>, <span class="pl-v">quote</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">F</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Explore the GSEA plot of enrichment of the pathway-associated genes in the ranked list:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Plot the GSEA plot for a single enriched pathway, `hsa03040`
gseaplot(gseaKEGG, geneSetID = 'hsa03040')"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Plot the GSEA plot for a single enriched pathway, `hsa03040`</span>

<p dir="auto">Use the <a href="http://bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/pathview.html" rel="nofollow">Pathview R package</a> to integrate the KEGG pathway data from clusterProfiler into pathway images:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Output images for a single significant KEGG pathway
detach(&quot;package:dplyr&quot;, unload=TRUE) # first unload dplyr to avoid conflicts

              pathway.id = &quot;hsa03040&quot;,
              species = &quot;hsa&quot;,

<blockquote>
<p dir="auto"><strong>NOTE:</strong> Printing out Pathview images for all significant pathways can be easily performed as follows:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Output images for all significant KEGG pathways

</blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Instead of exploring enrichment of KEGG gene sets, we can also explore the enrichment of BP Gene Ontology terms using gene set enrichment analysis:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# GSEA using gene sets associated with BP Gene Ontology terms
gseaGO &lt;- gseGO(geneList = foldchanges,

              verbose = FALSE)

<p dir="auto">There are other gene sets available for GSEA analysis in clusterProfiler (Disease Ontology, Reactome pathways, etc.). In addition, it is possible to supply your own gene set GMT file, such as a GMT for MSigDB using special clusterProfiler functions as shown below:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="biocLite(&quot;GSEABase&quot;)
library(GSEABase)

# Load in GMT file of gene sets (we downloaded from the Broad Institute [website](http://software.broadinstitute.org/gsea/msigdb/collections.jsp) for MSigDB)

c2 &lt;- read.gmt(&quot;/data/c2.cp.v6.0.entrez.gmt.txt&quot;)

msig &lt;- GSEA(foldchanges, TERM2GENE=c2, verbose=FALSE)

msig_df &lt;- data.frame(msig)"><pre>biocLite(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>GSEABase<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">GSEABase</span>)

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Load in GMT file of gene sets (we downloaded from the Broad Institute [website](http://software.broadinstitute.org/gsea/msigdb/collections.jsp) for MSigDB)</span>

<span class="pl-smi">c2</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> read.gmt(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>/data/c2.cp.v6.0.entrez.gmt.txt<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)

<span class="pl-smi">msig</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> GSEA(<span class="pl-smi">foldchanges</span>, <span class="pl-v">TERM2GENE</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-smi">c2</span>, <span class="pl-v">verbose</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">FALSE</span>)

<span class="pl-smi">msig_df</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-k">data.frame</span>(<span class="pl-smi">msig</span>)</pre></div>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-pathway-topology-tools" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#pathway-topology-tools"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Pathway topology tools</h2>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/pathway_analysis.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/pathway_analysis.png" alt="Pathway analysis tools" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<p dir="auto">The last main type of functional analysis technique is pathway topology analysis. Pathway topology analysis often takes into account gene interaction information along with the fold changes and adjusted p-values from differential expression analysis to identify dysregulated pathways. Depending on the tool, pathway topology tools explore how genes interact with each other (e.g. activation, inhibition, phosphorylation, ubiquitination, etc.) to determine the pathway-level statistics. Pathway topology-based methods utilize the number and type of interactions between gene product (our DE genes) and other gene products to infer gene function or pathway association.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-spia" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#spia"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>SPIA</h3>
<p dir="auto">The <a href="http://bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/SPIA.html" rel="nofollow">SPIA (Signaling Pathway Impact Analysis)</a> tool can be used to integrate the lists of differentially expressed genes, their fold changes, and pathway topology to identify affected pathways. The blog post from <a href="http://www.gettinggeneticsdone.com/2012/03/pathway-analysis-for-high-throughput.html" rel="nofollow">Getting Genetics Done</a> provides a step-by-step procedure for using and understanding SPIA.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Set-up

source(&quot;http://bioconductor.org/biocLite.R&quot;) 
biocLite(&quot;SPIA&quot;)
library(SPIA)

## Significant genes is a vector of fold changes where the names are ENTREZ gene IDs. The background set is a vector of all the genes represented on the platform.

background_entrez &lt;- res_entrez$entrez

sig_res_entrez &lt;- res_entrez[which(res_entrez$padj &lt; 0.05), ]

sig_entrez &lt;- sig_res_entrez$log2FoldChange

names(sig_entrez) &lt;- sig_res_entrez$entrez

head(sig_entrez)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Set-up</span>

source(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>http://bioconductor.org/biocLite.R<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>) 
biocLite(<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>SPIA<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)
library(<span class="pl-smi">SPIA</span>)

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Significant genes is a vector of fold changes where the names are ENTREZ gene IDs. The background set is a vector of all the genes represented on the platform.</span>

<span class="pl-smi">background_entrez</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">entrez</span>

<span class="pl-smi">sig_res_entrez</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span>[which(<span class="pl-smi">res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">padj</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;</span> <span class="pl-c1">0.05</span>), ]

<span class="pl-smi">sig_entrez</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">sig_res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">log2FoldChange</span>

names(<span class="pl-smi">sig_entrez</span>) <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> <span class="pl-smi">sig_res_entrez</span><span class="pl-k">$</span><span class="pl-smi">entrez</span>

head(<span class="pl-smi">sig_entrez</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Now that we have our background and significant genes in the appropriate format, we can run SPIA:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="
spia_result &lt;- spia(de=sig_entrez, all=background_entrez, organism=&quot;hsa&quot;)

head(spia_result, n=20)"><pre><span class="pl-smi">spia_result</span> <span class="pl-k">&lt;-</span> spia(<span class="pl-v">de</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-smi">sig_entrez</span>, <span class="pl-v">all</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-smi">background_entrez</span>, <span class="pl-v">organism</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>hsa<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)

head(<span class="pl-smi">spia_result</span>, <span class="pl-v">n</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">20</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">SPIA outputs a table showing significantly dysregulated pathways based on over-representation and signaling perturbations accumulation. The table shows the following information:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><code>pSize</code>: the number of genes on the pathway</li>
<li><code>NDE</code>: the number of DE genes per pathway</li>
<li><code>tA</code>: the observed total perturbation accumulation in the pathway</li>
<li><code>pNDE</code>: the probability to observe at least NDE genes on the pathway using a hypergeometric model (similar to ORA)</li>
<li><code>pPERT</code>: the probability to observe a total accumulation more extreme than tA only by chance</li>
<li><code>pG</code>: the p-value obtained by combining pNDE and pPERT</li>
<li><code>pGFdr</code> and <code>pGFWER</code> are the False Discovery Rate and Bonferroni adjusted global p-values, respectively</li>
<li><code>Status</code>: gives the direction in which the pathway is perturbed (activated or inhibited)</li>
<li><code>KEGGLINK</code> gives a web link to the KEGG website that <strong>displays the pathway image</strong> with the differentially expressed genes highlighted in red</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">We can view the significantly dysregulated pathways by viewing the over-representation and perturbations for each pathway.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="plotP(spia_result, threshold=0.05)"><pre>plotP(<span class="pl-smi">spia_result</span>, <span class="pl-v">threshold</span><span class="pl-k">=</span><span class="pl-c1">0.05</span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">In this plot, each pathway is a point and the coordinates are the log of pNDE (using a hypergeometric model) and the p-value from perturbations, pPERT. The oblique lines in the plot show the significance regions based on the combined evidence.</p>
<p dir="auto">If we choose to explore the significant genes from our dataset occurring in these pathways, we can subset our SPIA results:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-r notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="## Look at pathway 03013 and view kegglink
subset(spia_result, ID == &quot;03013&quot;)"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># Look at pathway 03013 and view kegglink</span>
subset(<span class="pl-smi">spia_result</span>, <span class="pl-smi">ID</span> <span class="pl-k">==</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>03013<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span>)</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Then, click on the <a href="http://www.genome.jp/dbget-bin/show_pathway?hsa03013+5901+7514+4686+51808+1207+25929+50628+79760+11171+3837+10073+9939+9775+22985+10921+10482+56000+5411+10189+29107+55916+23165+23511+9688+53371+10762+59343+4928+6396+57122+79902+81929+8480+55746+23225+100101267+94026+9883+8021+4927+7329+5905+6612+10419+57510+1915+1917+51068+5976+84305+10209+10289+8661+8662+8666+8667+8668+8669+10556+10775+10799+10940+11102+9984+57187+80145+132430+26986+5042+80336+8894+10605+1981+1982+8672+1983+1975+10460+9669+1967+8890+8892+8893+26999+2332+9513" rel="nofollow">KEGGLINK</a>, we can view the genes within our dataset from these perturbed pathways:</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/hsa05222.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/hsa05222.png" alt="perturbed_pathway" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<hr>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-other-tools" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#other-tools"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Other Tools</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-genemania" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#genemania"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>GeneMANIA</h3>
<p dir="auto"><a href="http://genemania.org/" rel="nofollow">GeneMANIA</a> is a tool for predicting the function of your genes. Rather than looking for enrichment, the query gene set is evaluated in the context of curated functional association data and results are displayed in the form of a network. Association data include protein and genetic interactions, pathways, co-expression, co-localization and protein domain similarity. Genes are represented as the nodes of the network and edges are formed by known association evidence. The query gene set is highlighted and so you can find other genes that are related based on the toplogy in the network. This tool is more useful for smaller gene sets (&lt; 400 genes), as you can see in the figure below our input results in a bit of a hairball that is hard to interpret.</p>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/blob/master/img/genemania.png"><img src="/hbctraining/DGE_workshop/raw/master/img/genemania.png" alt="genemania" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Use the significant gene list generated from the analysis we performed in class as input to GeneMANIA. Using only pathway and coexpression data as evidence, take a look at the network that results. Can you predict anything functionally from this set of genes?</p>
</blockquote>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-co-expression-clustering" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#co-expression-clustering"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Co-expression clustering</h3>
<p dir="auto">Co-expression clustering is often used to identify genes of novel pathways or networks by grouping genes together based on similar trends in expression. These tools are useful in identifying genes in a pathway, when their participation in a pathway and/or the pathway itself is unknown. These tools cluster genes with similar expression patterns to create 'modules' of co-expressed genes which often reflect functionally similar groups of genes. These 'modules' can then be compared across conditions or in a time-course experiment to identify any biologically relevant pathway or network information.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can visualize co-expression clustering using heatmaps, which should be viewed as suggestive only; serious classification of genes needs better methods.</p>
<p dir="auto">The way the tools perform clustering is by taking the entire expression matrix and computing pair-wise co-expression values. A network is then generated from which we explore the topology to make inferences on gene co-regulation. The <a href="http://www.genetics.ucla.edu/labs/horvath/CoexpressionNetwork" rel="nofollow">WGCNA</a> package (in R) is one example of a more sophisticated method for co-expression clustering.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-resources-for-functional-analysis" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#resources-for-functional-analysis"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Resources for functional analysis</h2>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>g:Profiler - <a href="http://biit.cs.ut.ee/gprofiler/index.cgi" rel="nofollow">http://biit.cs.ut.ee/gprofiler/index.cgi</a></li>
<li>DAVID - <a href="http://david.abcc.ncifcrf.gov/tools.jsp" rel="nofollow">http://david.abcc.ncifcrf.gov/tools.jsp</a></li>
<li>clusterProfiler - <a href="http://bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/clusterProfiler.html" rel="nofollow">http://bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/clusterProfiler.html</a></li>
<li>GeneMANIA - <a href="http://www.genemania.org/" rel="nofollow">http://www.genemania.org/</a></li>
<li>GenePattern -  <a href="http://www.broadinstitute.org/cancer/software/genepattern/" rel="nofollow">http://www.broadinstitute.org/cancer/software/genepattern/</a> (need to register)</li>
<li>WebGestalt - <a href="http://bioinfo.vanderbilt.edu/webgestalt/" rel="nofollow">http://bioinfo.vanderbilt.edu/webgestalt/</a> (need to register)</li>
<li>AmiGO - <a href="http://amigo.geneontology.org/amigo" rel="nofollow">http://amigo.geneontology.org/amigo</a></li>
<li>ReviGO (visualizing GO analysis, input is GO terms) - <a href="http://revigo.irb.hr/" rel="nofollow">http://revigo.irb.hr/</a></li>
<li>WGCNA - <a href="http://www.genetics.ucla.edu/labs/horvath/CoexpressionNetwork" rel="nofollow">http://www.genetics.ucla.edu/labs/horvath/CoexpressionNetwork</a></li>
<li>GSEA - <a href="http://software.broadinstitute.org/gsea/index.jsp" rel="nofollow">http://software.broadinstitute.org/gsea/index.jsp</a></li>
<li>SPIA - <a href="https://www.bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/SPIA.html" rel="nofollow">https://www.bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/SPIA.html</a></li>
<li>GAGE/Pathview - <a href="http://www.bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/gage.html" rel="nofollow">http://www.bioconductor.org/packages/release/bioc/html/gage.html</a></li>
</ul>
<hr>
